    <li> My original review is below.  All that was true until recently.  I had the scale for about 6 weeks then suddenly and for no apparent reason it will no longer lock onto a weight. It wasn&#x27;t even in a damp bathroom.  I kept it in the bedroom on a hardwood floor.  Just one day it worked great and the next time I used it a few days later, I couldn&#x27;t get a reading.  It lasted just long enough to prevent me from getting a refund.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Once you&#x27;ve gotten past the confusing set up instructions this is a very nice scale.  A label on it tells you to \\&quot;auto-calibrate\\&quot; and says, \\&quot;Place scale on floor and allow to turn off without stepping on the scale\\&quot;.  Huh?  It doesn&#x27;t even go on w/o stepping on it, so how can you \\&quot;allow it to turn off\\&quot;?  The separate instructions inside the box say that each time you move it you should turn it on by stepping on it, then letting it turn off after \\&quot;or the scale will add its own weight\\&quot; to the number displayed.  (And give the person getting weighed a panic attack.)  Turns out, what these two things mean is that after the first time you put it down for use, and every time you lift it to clean or to move it somewhere else, you have to step on briefly, just long enough for the display to read \\&quot;00\\&quot; &amp; not long enough to show a weight, and get right off, leaving it alone until the display goes dark.  From then on until you pick it up again it will stay correctly calibrated.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Nice things about it: it comes w/ its own batteries; it&#x27;s fashionably thin; it&#x27;s large enough for the display to be visible even if you&#x27;ve got a bit of a belly; the display is well-lit and large; the display stays on for about 20 seconds after you get off so if you are too big to see it when you&#x27;re on the scale, you can still see what you weigh; it doesn&#x27;t wobble even if the floor is not absolutely flat; it doesn&#x27;t have a bunch of excess functions most of us don&#x27;t want b/c if we&#x27;re obsessive enough to be weighing ourselves at home we don&#x27;t need a scale to track our weight (do you really want to have to tell it each time that it&#x27;s you &amp; not your SO being weighed b/c it&#x27;s tracking 2 people&#x27;s weights?).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;While I can&#x27;t swear it&#x27;s accurate, the weights I&#x27;ve been getting seem to make sense.  Can&#x27;t think of any negatives, but I don&#x27;t yet know about its durability.</li>

    <li> O.K., it&#x27;s just a Digital Scale for home usage right...  My mission was to give my wife a Digital Scale as a nice surprise gift.  Well after looking &amp; reviewing the dozens of makes, models, reviews, pricing, perceived quality of manufacture, etc. in Amazon... I simply chose this model.  I have an Electronics Engineering background, and believe they are all made in China (big surprise, right), and they probably all have the same -or nearly the same- \\&quot;Strain/Weight Pressure Sensor Piezoelectric Crystals\\&quot; (that&#x27;s the actual \\&quot;techno\\&quot; for how most all these type scales work) which converts Mechanical Forces (weight) into an Electrical force (voltage &amp; current), that feeds the Electronic Measuring Circuitry.  The batteries (2 AAA type) are primarily used for the Digital LED numerical display.    So O.K., now that you have, but did not ask for, or need to know \\&quot;how they work\\&quot;... Bottom line, hey this Scale works, reads very accurate, nice Blue Numbers, is aesthetically nice looking, and the wife is happy!   Hence a winner.</li>

    <li> This is by far the best weighing machine I&#x27;ve ever owned and I totally love the slim form factor. So much so that the slim form factor is an inspiration to become slimmer :-)&lt;br /&gt;Jokes apart, the machine is accurate and quite effective. I did have an initial scare because the weight on this was almost 6 pounds lower than the weight on my office weighing machine. However, I soon realized the extra weight is usually due to the extra layer of clothing plus the paraphernalia (wallets/cell phones etc) which one typically carries. I tried weighing myself before leaving for office (in complete attire) and the weight was within the margin of error. That apart, I like the large blue LED display, the fact that I don&#x27;t have to tap on it before I stand on it and that it&#x27;s extremely light (Makes it much more convenient to stash or store).&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;One of the bigger concerns which people have raised about this weighing machine is the inaccuracy of results or inconsistent operation. I believe this is not a generic problem with the design of this weighing machine but more of a quality control issue. Some people may take this negatively, but one has to understand that it&#x27;s almost impossible to have 100% quality control. The cost of increasing quality control from say 99.5% to 99.9% may be so prohibitive that it may not be practical for either the seller or the buyer. And that&#x27;s just not true of a cheap weighing machine! In fact if you do have some time try reading some of the reviews on Canon L series lens (or equivalent ones from Nikon or any other brand). These are professional grade lens and usually cost upwards of a couple of grand, however even those it&#x27;s not uncommon to have the odd variant which doesn&#x27;t perform as well as it should. (The real professionals even have extensive setups to test the quality of the lens and may buy/replace 2 or 3 versions before they settle on one). So what can we do as customers, just count our losses and move on? Well that&#x27;s where Amazon comesto rescue, they have this amazing 30 day &#x27;no-questions-asked&#x27; return policy (And if any Amazon reps are reading this, I love you guys for it!!) which even covers shipping. For those that care to read further, here is my overall impression...In case you haven&#x27;t noticed there are multiple scales being sold on Amazon right now by numerous companies.  Its almost as if there is some sort a cut throat scale industry fighting tooth and nail for your dollar.  Who knew?  I read through many of the reviews and I was lead to believe the Omega Ultra Slim Digital Bathroom Scale would meet my needs.  I was wrong and sorely misled.  I had 4 requirements when shopping for a scale:  1. It has to be a material other than glass.  I have small children and a glass scale would inevitably lead to a broken scale and mostly likely tears and blood.  Therefore, glass was not an option.  2.  It could not be big and bulky.  I wanted a low profile scale I didn&#x27;t have to constantly move around my bathroom.  3.  It had to have a highly visible display.  At 5:30AM or 10:00PM I don&#x27;t want to strain my eyes or put on my glasses to read the scale.  4.  Finally, the most important feature of all, it must be consistently accurate.  This scale met the first three requirements easily.  It seems to be constructed of quality plastic.  I was able to place it in a location on the floor where it is unobstructed by the bathroom door opening.  It has a beautiful large display that is easy to see.  Unfortunately, that&#x27;s where the positives end.  This scale failed the last test, accuracy.  This scale is not accurate.  If I step on the scale, I will get one reading.  When it goes blank and I step on it again within seconds, it is almost as if it has an internal memoryand gives the exact same reading.  If I step on the scale 3 minutes later, I get a completely different reading.  This happens repeatedly.  To test the accuracy of the scale, I placed a 75lb dumbbell on the scale three different times.  First reading was 72.8lbs, Second reading was 73, Third reading was 73.4.  This scale just isn&#x27;t consistently accurate.  Some might think my review is a bit unfair, seeing as how the scale meets three out of my four criteria.  Perhaps, but I bought a scale and the purpose of a scale is to accurately measure weight.  When a product fails at its primary purpose, then it doesn&#x27;t deserve a rating above 1 star.  So, if you are looking for a scale that will give you a ball park weight, then this might work for you.  If you want a scale that gives you an accurate and consistent weight, look elsewhere.</li>
    <li> I give this scale a 5 star rating.  It is thin, weighs in .2 pound increments, and is easy to read  with large black on blue numbering. And, it is well-priced.  If you&#x27;re looking for a scale, look no further.</li>
